It keeps this connection open and reuses it in subsequent requests.\\n52: Django closes the connection once it exceeds the maximum age defined by\\n53: :setting:`CONN_MAX_AGE` or when it isn't usable any longer.\\n54: \\n55: In detail, Django automatically opens a connection to the database whenever it\\n56: needs one and doesn't have one already — either because this is the first\\n57: connection, or because the previous connection was closed.\\n58: \\n59: At the beginning of each request, Django closes the connection if it has\\n60: reached its maximum age. It keeps this connection open and reuses it in subsequent requests.\\n52: Django closes the connection once it exceeds the maximum age defined by\\n53: :setting:`CONN_MAX_AGE` or when it isn't usable any longer.\\n54: \\n55: In detail, Django automatically opens a connection to the database whenever it\\n56: needs one and doesn't have one already — either because this is the first\\n57: connection, or because the previous connection was closed.\\n58: \\n59: At the beginning of each request, Django closes the connection if it has\\n60: reached its maximum age. If your database terminates idle connections after\\n61: some time, you should set :setting:`CONN_MAX_AGE` to a lower value, so that\\n62: Django doesn't attempt to use a connection that has been terminated by the\\n63: database server. If your database terminates idle connections after\\n61: some time, you should set :setting:`CONN_MAX_AGE` to a lower value, so that\\n62: Django doesn't attempt to use a connection that has been terminated by the\\n63: database server. (This problem may only affect very low traffic sites.)\\n64: \",\"endLine\":64,\"startLine\":49},{\"content\":\"38: The default value is ``0``, preserving the historical behavior of closing the\\n39: database connection at the end of each request. It keeps this connection open and reuses it in subsequent requests.\\n52: Django closes the connection once it exceeds the maximum age defined by\\n53: :setting:`CONN_MAX_AGE` or when it isn't usable any longer.\\n54: \\n55: In detail, Django automatically opens a connection to the database whenever it\\n56: needs one and doesn't have one already — either because this is the first\\n57: connection, or because the previous connection was closed.\\n58: \\n59: At the beginning of each request, Django closes the connection if it has\\n60: reached its maximum age. If your database terminates idle connections after\\n61: some time, you should set :setting:`CONN_MAX_AGE` to a lower value, so that\\n62: Django doesn't attempt to use a connection that has been terminated by the\\n63: database server. (This problem may only affect very low traffic sites.)\\n64: \",\"endLine\":64,\"startLine\":49},{\"content\":\"38: The default value is ``0``, preserving the historical behavior of closing the\\n39: database connection at the end of each request. To enable persistent\\n40: connections, set :setting:`CONN_MAX_AGE` to a positive integer of seconds. For\\n41: unlimited persistent connections, set it to ``None``.\\n42: \\n43: When using ASGI, persistent connections should be disabled. Instead, use your\\n44: database backend's built-in connection pooling if available, or investigate a\\n45: third-party connection pooling option if required.\\n46: \\n47: Connection management\\n48: ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\\n49: \",\"endLine\":49,\"startLine\":38},{\"content\":\"27: \\n28: .. _persistent-database-connections:\\n29: \\n30: Persistent connections\\n31: ----------------------\\n32: It keeps this connection open and reuses it in subsequent requests.\n52: Django closes the connection once it exceeds the maximum age defined by\n53: :setting:`CONN_MAX_AGE` or when it isn't usable any longer.\n54: \n55: In detail, Django automatically opens a connection to the database whenever it\n56: needs one and doesn't have one already — either because this is the first\n57: connection, or because the previous connection was closed.\n58: \n59: At the beginning of each request, Django closes the connection if it has\n60: reached its maximum age. If your database terminates idle connections after\n61: some time, you should set :setting:`CONN_MAX_AGE` to a lower value, so that\n62: Django doesn't attempt to use a connection that has been terminated by the\n63: database server. (This problem may only affect very low traffic sites.)\n64: ","endLine":64,"startLine":49},{"content":"38: The default value is ``0``, preserving the historical behavior of closing the\n39: database connection at the end of each request. To enable persistent\n40: connections, set :setting:`CONN_MAX_AGE` to a positive integer of seconds. For\n41: unlimited persistent connections, set it to ``None``.\n42: \n43: When using ASGI, persistent connections should be disabled. Instead, use your\n44: database backend's built-in connection pooling if available, or investigate a\n45: third-party connection pooling option if required.\n46: \n47: Connection management\n48: ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\n49: ","endLine":49,"startLine":38},{"content":"27: \n28: .. _persistent-database-connections:\n29: \n30: Persistent connections\n31: ----------------------\n32: The reported issue is:- Persistent connections (CONN_MAX_AGE = None) are being closed prematurely- Connections are being torn down after every request cycle- They're being closed \"as if CONN_MAX_AGE = 0\"\n\nLooking at the code:\n1. This is correct.For CONN_MAX_AGE = 0: close_at equals the current time, so the condition `time.monotonic() >= self.close_at` should be True, closing the connection.\n\nBut wait! If close_at = time.monotonic() (the current time when the connection is created), and we check `time.monotonic() >= self.close_at` in the very same moment, we get approximately:\n- T >= T, which is True\n\nSo the connection is closed immediately! This is NOT correct behavior for CONN_MAX_AGE = 0.
